  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1a0be24c-535e-4aab-a35b-ff5b3d819a82'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer4295835979431927331">Kyla is in danger from both the government Lorders who erased her memory and the terrorists who tried to use her. So now she’s on the run. Sporting a new identity and desperate to fill in the blank spaces of her life pre-Slating, Kyla heads to a remote mountain town to try to reunite with the birth mother she was kidnapped from as a child. There she is hoping all the piece</span>
  <span id="freeText4295835979431927331" style="display:none">Kyla is in danger from both the government Lorders who erased her memory and the terrorists who tried to use her. So now she’s on the run. Sporting a new identity and desperate to fill in the blank spaces of her life pre-Slating, Kyla heads to a remote mountain town to try to reunite with the birth mother she was kidnapped from as a child. There she is hoping all the pieces of her life will come together and she can finally take charge of her own future. But even in the idyllic wilderness and the heart of her original family, Kyla realizes there is no escape from the oppressive Lorders. Someone close to her may be one of them, and even more frighteningly, her birth mother has been keeping secrets of her own.<br /><br />In this stunning series finale, Kyla finally finds out who she really is, and the road to this discovery, and to deciding who she wants to become, is full of dangerous twists and turns that will keep readers riveted.</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_801708504" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/801708504" />
    <a title="Nea Barabea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6151318-nea-barabea"><img alt="Nea Barabea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1370085237p2/6151318.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/801708504?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nea Barabea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nea Barabea" href="/user/show/6151318-nea-barabea">Nea Barabea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer801708504" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9263449826866988804">Holy shit. Through the first half of the book I could't help myself but wonder, how will Teri Terry wrap it all up in so little time and space? Man, I was so wrong. She's done it perfectly. SO perfectly I was speechless till the end. Well, with the occasional crying and sobbing. Cause I did cry. This is one of the best dystopian books I've ever read. And that's a fact.<br/><br/>Kyla. Rain. Lucy. Riley. I'll stick with Kyla. This girl, I cannot believe all that she went through and she was still standing. </span>
  <span id="freeText9263449826866988804" style="display:none">Holy shit. Through the first half of the book I could't help myself but wonder, how will Teri Terry wrap it all up in so little time and space? Man, I was so wrong. She's done it perfectly. SO perfectly I was speechless till the end. Well, with the occasional crying and sobbing. Cause I did cry. This is one of the best dystopian books I've ever read. And that's a fact.<br /><br />Kyla. Rain. Lucy. Riley. I'll stick with Kyla. This girl, I cannot believe all that she went through and she was still standing. We can call it courage, but I will call it determination. Wow. Really, Kyla in this book was totally badass. Gone is the scared girl full of doubts and fears. In this book we are faced with a Kyla who is strong, determinated, courageous, brave, smart and still fast at running. <br /><br />I actually changed my mind about the boy.. and that doesn't happen often ;)<br /><br />The writing was stunning! And so realistic. Really, I could see it in my mind. Everything, and let me tell you, it was pretty terrifying. I could feel my heart beating so fast, the adrenaline pumping through my body and the feeling was as scary as it was exhilarating! And I quite forgot how amazing it feels to look at the clock and see it 5am and not being bothered about it at all. Some thing are worth it. And Shattered definitely is!<br /><br />Shattered is an amazing conclusion to an amazing trilogy! Slated was awesome, Fractured was incredible, but Shattered takes the whole serie to a whole new level. So, if you haven't yet picked this serie up, I highly suggest you to do it ASAP! It's goddamn worth it!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9263449826866988804" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13841746820346600309">Hmmmm, if I was being fair, I would'be given it a 3.8 stars rating and rounded it to four, but the ending just killed everything to me, so it's a 3.5 star rating rounded down. Whatever.<br/><br/>The whole book was pretty fabulous, but the ending just killed it. And the romance wasn't so great in general.<br/><br/>First off, this was much more engaging than the other two books. I don't know why. Maybe it's because the stakes were higher or something, but it was just more addictive. This world, with slating and every</span>
  <span id="freeText13841746820346600309" style="display:none">Hmmmm, if I was being fair, I would'be given it a 3.8 stars rating and rounded it to four, but the ending just killed everything to me, so it's a 3.5 star rating rounded down. Whatever.<br /><br />The whole book was pretty fabulous, but the ending just killed it. And the romance wasn't so great in general.<br /><br />First off, this was much more engaging than the other two books. I don't know why. Maybe it's because the stakes were higher or something, but it was just more addictive. This world, with slating and everything is pretty cool. I'm not big on reading dystopian novels, but I like this one. Overall, I would say that it's a nice ending. So here comes the spoilery stuff:<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So there's like a love triangle now, with Aiden and Ben. WHAT?????? I have no idea why Kyla/Rain/Riley still likes him. Like seriously. In the first book, their romance was just cute, in the second book, they only had like one scene together, and she still held onto hope, and in the final book, she only meets him at the end and she's all over him again, and even when he betrays her, she still ends up choosing him, the starcrossed lover, instead of the super awesome guy, Aiden, who loves her and cares for her. Actually really cares for her, unlike Ben who runs off at the end. Okay, maybe she does actually end up with Aiden at the end, since they hug and Ben is gone, but I thought that it was a total butthole thing to do to just drive away one day. Likes seriously. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Also, introducing a love triangle in the final book??????????? So not cool. <br /><br />Even with that, I loved the action and all the revelations and everything. But the romance (and the ending) just killed everything. And the ending was also predictable.<br /></span>

<div id="review_714477917" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/714477917" />
    <a title="tthepageturner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2428631-tthepageturner"><img alt="tthepageturner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1467037437p2/2428631.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/714477917?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="tthepageturner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="tthepageturner" href="/user/show/2428631-tthepageturner">tthepageturner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer714477917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16879836067318454006">As far as conclusions to trilogies go Shattered was a good one.<br/><br/>Kyla is still wound up about what happened to Ben, and although I felt sorry for her I wasn't actually too bothered about Ben. Why? Because I wasn't emotionally invested in the romance between Ben and Kyla in book one. It was dull and so was Ben to be honest. For this reason, as harsh as it may sound to some, I didn't really care much about what happened to him.<br/><br/>I was, however, pleased with the way Aiden and Kyla's relationship evolve</span>
  <span id="freeText16879836067318454006" style="display:none">As far as conclusions to trilogies go Shattered was a good one.<br /><br />Kyla is still wound up about what happened to Ben, and although I felt sorry for her I wasn't actually too bothered about Ben. Why? Because I wasn't emotionally invested in the romance between Ben and Kyla in book one. It was dull and so was Ben to be honest. For this reason, as harsh as it may sound to some, I didn't really care much about what happened to him.<br /><br />I was, however, pleased with the way Aiden and Kyla's relationship evolved. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[He was the guy I was rooting for as a love interest, and although Kyla was pretty much oblivious to his feelings until the very end I am glad that the book hinted at a future for the two of them. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> One thing I appreciated about Aiden was that he completely supported Kyla, without being pushy or condescending. In contrast to Ben, he was a fully developed character.<br /><br />Many of the long awaited answers to questions readers have dying to know are answered in this book. Kyla's journey of self discovery continues and she finally learns the truth about her past. If there was only one thing I could say about this book it would be that there is no lack of character development on the part of the mc. She grows and grows, coming out stronger in the end. Furthermore, Terry's writing style really adds to the horrors of what goes down in this book, adding tension and edge to the story. The freakiest thing about this trilogy is that it seems realistic, like the events that took place could actually happen. <br /><br />In an overcrowded genre, Slated is a unique dystopian trilogy. <br /><br />This review also appears on my blog, <a href="http://tthepageturner.blogspot.co.uk/2014/04/shattered-by-teri-terry.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Page Turner</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16879836067318454006" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1409168207" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14970424769549952987">“I have both been given and taken so many identities, but at last I am beginning to grow into my one true name.<br/>This was the gift my mother gave to me: Hope.” <br/>― Teri Terry, Shattered<br/><br/><br/>You guys have to read this! An excellent conclusion to an excellent series, One of the best dystopians out there! Lovely.</span>

<div id="review_1615989259" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1615989259" />
    <a title="Livia Winata" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27539260-livia-winata"><img alt="Livia Winata" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571818867p2/27539260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1615989259?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Livia Winata" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Livia Winata" href="/user/show/27539260-livia-winata">Livia Winata</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9786022498261" href="/book/show/28187323-shattered">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27539260-livia-winata?shelf=a-decent-reading">a-decent-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27539260-livia-winata?shelf=series-novel">series-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27539260-livia-winata?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27539260-livia-winata?shelf=suspense-thriller">suspense-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27539260-livia-winata?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27539260-livia-winata?shelf=f-urban">f-urban</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27539260-livia-winata?shelf=on-shelf">on-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27539260-livia-winata?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27539260-livia-winata?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1615989259" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6181396848484411013"><b>
  <blockquote> ONE OF THE BEST POST-APOCALYPTIC DYSTOPIA TRILOGY ! </blockquote>
</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  
</blockquote><br/><blockquote>
  
</blockquote><br/><br/>It surprised me in the way no other book did before. <i>It really TERRIFIC. </i> What the hell with all about twisted and complicated mystery. OMG, I never did a right guessing. All little thing in this book was amazingly complete all the puzzle in my head. It's a <b>VERY STUNNING WRAP UP OF THE TRILOGY</b>.<br/><br/>Well, what can I say. The idea, the starting, the ending, the plot, the characters, and all of them are great. I could write a review but I </span>
  <span id="freeText6181396848484411013" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote> ONE OF THE BEST POST-APOCALYPTIC DYSTOPIA TRILOGY ! </blockquote>
</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  
</blockquote><br /><blockquote>
  
</blockquote><br /><br />It surprised me in the way no other book did before. <i>It really TERRIFIC. </i> What the hell with all about twisted and complicated mystery. OMG, I never did a right guessing. All little thing in this book was amazingly complete all the puzzle in my head. It's a <b>VERY STUNNING WRAP UP OF THE TRILOGY</b>.<br /><br />Well, what can I say. The idea, the starting, the ending, the plot, the characters, and all of them are great. I could write a review but I will not able to praise this trilogy, this book especially. I wasn't so sure how it gonna end after a whole long roller coaster rides. But who knows, it really end very well that one will be so surprised.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  
</blockquote><br /><br />Here I start with the starting. <b> It started slow in a good way. </b> It gave me a big question mark in my head, how can Teri Terry end this if the story was went out of the storyline? The slow pace continued in about one third of the book. Then everything came up, every puzzles was revealed and placed. All about Kyla's past was already settled. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><br />Kyla was a name of a girl that was <pre> SLATED </pre>. She didn't know about her past at all. Then gradually, the memories she had was appeared. First of all is when she found out that she is a left handed rather than a right handed. Well, she could use both hands actually. But when she underwent the <pre> SLATED </pre> procedure, she was diagnosed to be right handed. So the part that was <pre> SLATED </pre> was the time she was right handed. The left handed memories, came up, because it never meant to be <pre> SLATED </pre>. <br /><br />Her consciousness appeared. She has two past. One is up until she's 10 years old named Lucy. Lucy was a happy girl living with her dad (and mom actually but the memories of her mom didn't appear at all). Then one day she was kidnapped by Anti Governor Terrorist (<pre>AGT</pre>). <pre>AGT</pre> was an organization that attempted to take down the Governor today. The Governor today was awful. It's leaded by a prime minister and helped by so many <pre> Inspectors </pre>. The <pre> Inspectors </pre> was feared by people in country as they always seemed to take people out then the people theirself gone. So the AGT took little Lucy for being the terrorist, the key of its success. Lucy was taught to be a left handed. This personality wasn't <pre> SLATED </pre>. So she gradually knew about her past when she was in AGT in 11-15 years old.<br /><br />After being <pre> SLATED </pre>, she lived with her adoptive parents and another <pre> SLATED </pre> sister. Her adoptive mother, Sandra was the daughter of the first prime minister who created the <pre> Inspectors </pre> and all the rule. She found List of Missing People (<pre> LMP </pre>) through her adoptive sister, Amy. Amy's boyfriend, Jazz, had a cousin named, Mac. Mac was one of the <pre> LMP </pre>. So she found out about her past's identity.<br /><br />When her memories gradually revealed. She met this man named Nico. Nico was likely the <pre> AGT </pre>'s leader. So Kyla joined to <pre>AGT</pre> to follow its plan to make a better England without <pre> Inspectors </pre>. Then in the end, she found out she was being used by AGT. She wished to be a suicide bomber.<br /><br />Then in the last book, she found out she was an adopted daughter, also. She was being used by <pre> Inspectors </pre> which is her grandmother. The grandmother gave Kyla to her "was-known-as" birth mother. As she was in mourning of losing her first daughter, she made Kyla as she's her own daughter. Kyla, named Lucy. Then all what happen to little Lucy next was how <pre>AGT</pre> cooperated with <pre> Inspectors </pre>.<br /><br />In the end, Kyla's finally know that her true birth mother is the daughter of the prime minister. She was dead for being a member of the current government refused unrest. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><blockquote>
  
</blockquote><br /><br />Then the wrapped up was half of the book left. I was wondered how everything gonna end in such few pages. But OMG, <b> TERI TERRY NAILED THE ENDING, also </b>. She made everything in sense. How come everything became connected to each other that well. I love the ending. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">["HOPE", Kyla's true birth name.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I never imagined it will ended like this. I'm still in shock. It's soooo unpredictable yet so sweet.<br /><br />In this book, don't hope for romance. Romance was such a bullshit. Her romantic partner ended betray her. Then an unpredictable character that never be counted at first became the good guy. OMG, it's so twisted I couldn't even think about it to be like this. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><br />Ben, her boyfriend in SLATED was known to be trained in one of Inspector's training camp. He was so stupid in the book one, that I hoped he wasn't the main character of Kyla's romantic partner. Fortunately, he isn't. He betrayed Kyla for being one of an Inspector's spy along with his ex-girlfriend, Tori. Then Ben killed all the <pre> LMP </pre> member.What an unexpected ending, right? A boy with an excellent figure, known usually to be the main character became the bad character.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><blockquote>
  
</blockquote><br /><br />The characters weren't flat. <b> All people in this book was in deep character </b>. They're somehow so unpredictable. One can be so good then became bad. One can be sooo good that I almost cry losing them. But most of all, I love how Teri Terry worked with Kyla's personality. Lucy is innocent and brilliant. Rain is strong. Then Kyla searched through all the characters for being her now.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  
</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b> I RECOMMEND THIS BOOK TO ALL BOOK LOVER!! I LOVE IT AND HOPE YOU WILL ALSO DO </b>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="6181396848484411013" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Below" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8801338-below"><img alt="Below" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1042582780?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Below" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Below" href="/user/show/8801338-below">Below</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8801338-below?shelf=3-library-books">3-library-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8801338-below?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8801338-below?shelf=dystopia-and-crapsack-world">dystopia-and-crapsack-world</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1042582780" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11294348530147447028">1/5, 1.5/5 if I’m a little generous (this is probably a little better than say, The Cure or Allegiant). I wasn’t impressed with the ending to this series. I gave the first two books 2.5/5; I was not a huge fan but there were some things that I liked about it. I didn’t get on with this one nearly as well though I disliked the first half of the novel much more than the second. Spoileriffic review coming up.<br/><br/>The first argument I would make is related to the fact that the first section of the book fe</span>
  <span id="freeText11294348530147447028" style="display:none">1/5, 1.5/5 if I’m a little generous (this is probably a little better than say, The Cure or Allegiant). I wasn’t impressed with the ending to this series. I gave the first two books 2.5/5; I was not a huge fan but there were some things that I liked about it. I didn’t get on with this one nearly as well though I disliked the first half of the novel much more than the second. Spoileriffic review coming up.<br /><br />The first argument I would make is related to the fact that the first section of the book feels quite disconnected to what has happened so far. Kyla (or whatever you should call her) ends up in a completely different setting from the first two books. This is so that she can meet her mother Stella and find out more information from her about where she came from. My difficulty with the way that it was set up is that it is very difficult to pull off the main character meeting a bunch of new characters in the third book. It means that the characters that the reader had an interest in from the first two books generally get shoved out of the picture to focus on new characters that the reader does not care about because they haven’t built up a relationship with those characters. I understand the importance of Kyla meeting her mother and Stella was a new character who did need to come into it. However Kyla goes and stays in a boarding house with a bunch of new girls and these characters end up being characters that do not resonate with the reader given that we only have a few scenes to relate to the key girls at best. The key case I can think of to demonstrate this point is the case of Madison. Madison is a character who got on the wrong side of the wrong person and as a result she is arrested by the Lorders (one thing I like about these books: that term). But we only get a few scenes to know Madison so we don’t really care. Compare this to Ben being taken away in book one: we had the whole book to build up to the event so it invoked much more emotion in the reader. <br /><br />I felt that for the first half of the book, Kyla was incredibly insular, and it bothered me. All of the focus was upon who she was and finding everything out. I understand why that was the case, but it felt both excessively selfish and also inconsistent with Kyla as already established. In Fractured, Kyla makes several references in the text to Ben so that it’s clear that Ben is still in her thoughts. However, in Shattered, there’s a real lack of references to him (he’s mentioned only in the context of Madison’s man if I remember right) and there’s even fewer references to Mum and Amy. This makes Kyla feel even more disconnected from the characters that we had already met. Nico and Tori also had basically no presence. The withdrawn nature of Kyla bothered me because she was supposed to be getting to the point of questioning the Lorder society through the events of the previous novels but there’s no real element of that during the time she stays with Stella: 90% of the focus is on her personally, to the point where she is thinking about careers in serious terms. It isn’t until about the halfway point that this turns about and Kyla starts focussing on bringing down the Lorder government. This also makes the book feel disjointed. <br /><br />Regarding the second half of the novel, I am not sure I went along with everything that happened, but I’d like to pick up on one point in particular. I had real problems with how the author handled Tori. Here’s the rundown: in book 2 we find out that Tori was ‘rescued’ from death by a Lorder so he could take her back to his place and treat her like his sex slave. This makes Tori turn against the Lorder system and join the terrorists. However, Nico tells Tori that Kyla didn’t tell Tori that Ben was still alive and this makes Tori angry and she swears revenge. Following on from that, in book 3 Tori sides with the Lorder system in order to get revenge on Kyla. While I can understand her dislike of Kyla, I really do not find it plausible that someone would side with a system that was going to kill them and that was responsible for them being raped over Kyla just because Kyla didn’t tell her that Ben was alive. That’s ludicrous! I’m also tempted to argue that it’s rather misogynistic – of course a woman must put ~a man~ over everything else, even her own degradation. It reduces women to only caring about a relationship and makes Tori into another stereotypical and one-dimensional example of the ‘jealous bitch’ who’ll do anything to get the heroine’s man. It’s tedious at this point. I’m not that keen on what the author did with Nico either, but I can live with that element. But the way Tori is handled is beyond reason.<br /><br />The extra 0.5 I’m willing to give this is mainly because of Aiden and Mac and MIA. They are actually kind of cool. <br />I think I’ll leave it there as that covers the main flaws of this book. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11294348530147447028" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_742607842" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/742607842" />
    <a title="Carie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187401-carie"><img alt="Carie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1254869801p2/2187401.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/742607842?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carie" href="/user/show/2187401-carie">Carie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399161742" href="/book/show/18667841-shattered">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer742607842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13008508875631075973">Maybe 3.5 for this one… This book held my interest and had some tense, terrifying moments and some fascinating pieces to the whole puzzle of Kyla. BUT, I really hated how the romance was handled and I thought Kyla’s story got more and more convoluted and confusing as the story progressed, and the coincidences became REALLY ridiculous :(<br/><br/>I really HATED how <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Ben <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> was handled! I thought it was beyond obvious that <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[something weird was going on with him when </span></span>
  <span id="freeText13008508875631075973" style="display:none">Maybe 3.5 for this one… This book held my interest and had some tense, terrifying moments and some fascinating pieces to the whole puzzle of Kyla. BUT, I really hated how the romance was handled and I thought Kyla’s story got more and more convoluted and confusing as the story progressed, and the coincidences became REALLY ridiculous :(<br /><br />I really HATED how <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ben <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> was handled! I thought it was beyond obvious that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[something weird was going on with him when he and Kyla were first reunited <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>! And, though it really made me sad that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[he ended up betraying Kyla and the MIA <i>so thoroughly</i>--and that he ended up being a jerk in the end who Kyla never really <i>knew</i> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, I think I could have handled it all a bit better if <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Aiden had been presented as another option for Kyla MUCH earlier in this series--instead of all of the sudden in the last book--and if the author had shown some understandable reason why Kyla would have spent months with Ben at the end before he had his surgery… Was he repentant and actually acting like he wanted to be with her at that point? Or, was she just SO stubborn that she wouldn’t give up the hope that she’d get her “old Ben” back? This all came across as REALLY pathetic :( I think more should have been shown when Kyla and Ben first saw each other again after the big climax at the end… And, even though Aiden was such a latecomer as a love interest, he did really grow on me and I started rooting for him and I honestly couldn’t understand why Kyla wouldn’t have chosen him MUCH sooner :( Ben had to actually <i>steal a car</i> and desert her before she saw the light?!! Ridiculous! And, I was REALLY mad that we didn’t get some good romantic moments with Kyla and Aiden, if he’s who she was going to end up with :(  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>!! And, I have to say that I thought it was SUPER sad that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ben ended up as he did <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> at the end, too :( SO sad and disappointing!! I understand what the author was trying to do/say with the idea of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[people’s fundamental make-up not changing, regardless of Slating, and that you can’t <i>really</i> know someone when you (and they) don’t know their own past and who they really are. I also thought it was fascinating that Ben would end up really being a criminal after all. But, the whole thing with Ben was really depressing, too--especially that the only time he’d ever really been happy was when he was first Slated… I hated the way things turned out for Ben--and Ben and Kyla as a couple <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> :( The whole romantic storyline was just MADDENING and <i>very</i> disappointing!!<br /><br />I also thought a lot of the coincidences in the plot really stretched credibility and that Kyla’s many names and bizarre history became more and more convoluted and confusing as the story went along. The end of the book was REALLY intense and scary and I had no idea what would happen, but I ended up having a hard time believing the climax and resolution (<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the Prime Minister just happening to show up at Mac’s house at <i>just the right moment</i> to save Kyla--and then immediately resigning which magically "fixed" everything?! Hmmm...  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>) and untangling all the whys, whos, whats, and hows of the whole thing. I was very glad that the author provided some recap of previous books in this one, but it seemed like not everything fit just right or felt resolved/explained satisfactorily :(<br /><br />I did think the whole premise of this series was fascinating and I always loved the paranoid, “who can you trust?” vibe of these books. I also liked many of the characters, including Kyla herself. I loved that she would take action and that she always came across as a good, intelligent (<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[except where Ben and Aiden were concerned :(  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>), brave, strong person.<br /><br />Overall, I thought this was a fairly satisfying ending to the series, but I do wish a few things--the romance, in particular--had been different…<br /></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/792689082" />
    <a title="Shelley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3081722-shelley"><img alt="Shelley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420295300p2/3081722.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/792689082?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelley" href="/user/show/3081722-shelley">Shelley</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer792689082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1546805600663937837">Synopsis alert!<br/><br/>The gripping finale of the Slated trilogy!<br/><br/><br/><br/>Terrorists fractured Kyla’s mind. A tyrannical government erased her memories. And now she is on the run from both groups. She plans to start over with her recently discovered birth mother, Stella, trying to fill in the blank spaces of her life pre-slating. But there is no escape from the oppressive Lorders—Stella's mother is one of them, and that's not the only secret Stella's been keeping.<br/><br/>With her world turned upside-down once again, Kyl</span>
  <span id="freeText1546805600663937837" style="display:none">Synopsis alert!<br /><br />The gripping finale of the Slated trilogy!<br /><br /><br /><br />Terrorists fractured Kyla’s mind. A tyrannical government erased her memories. And now she is on the run from both groups. She plans to start over with her recently discovered birth mother, Stella, trying to fill in the blank spaces of her life pre-slating. But there is no escape from the oppressive Lorders—Stella's mother is one of them, and that's not the only secret Stella's been keeping.<br /><br />With her world turned upside-down once again, Kyla reaches her breaking point when she learns that children as young as four years old are being Slated. Resolving to stand up to the Lorders, Kyla is reunited with Ben, who doesn’t remember her, and Aiden, whose feelings about her seem to be changing.<br /><br />In the thrilling conclusion to this series of thought-provoking psychological thrillers, Teri Terry examines the role our memories play in our lives. She delivers a fast-paced read with a strong, proactive heroine, a disturbingly realistic future setting, and plot twists galore.</span>

<div id="review_1128558699" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1128558699" />
    <a title="Zuzana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17449341-zuzana"><img alt="Zuzana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546371474p2/17449341.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1128558699?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zuzana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zuzana" href="/user/show/17449341-zuzana">Zuzana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17449341-zuzana?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer8970686724986599627">*clap, clap, clap* <br/><br/>What a perfect ending to a perfect journey..<br/>I just need some time to process, and I'll have a review hopefully worthy of this amazing book. <br/><br/><b>-------- Edited</b><br/><br/>Let me just start by saying that Slated is one of the best dystopia trilogies I have ever read.   <span id="freeText8970686724986599627" style="display:none">*clap, clap, clap* <br /><br />What a perfect ending to a perfect journey..<br />I just need some time to process, and I'll have a review hopefully worthy of this amazing book. <br /><br /><b>-------- Edited</b><br /><br />Let me just start by saying that Slated is one of the best dystopia trilogies I have ever read. FACT.<br /><br />Book #3, SHATTERED, wraps up the story perfectly and we finally get all the answers. With so many plot twists, it's so easy to lose yourself in the story. <br />Kyla, Rain, Lucy, and her new identity in this book: Riley Kain, is a girl who went to hell and back so many times and was still standing. Despite everything she went through, all the lying and deceiving, and all the betrayal and memory loss, she still had courage and determination and <i> Hope </i>. In this book the scared girl full of doubts and fears is gone. In this book we are faced with a Kyla who is strong, determined, courageous, brave, smart and still fast at running. <br />--------------------------------------<br />The lorders and AGT think that Kayla is dead, but she's not. And with the help of Aiden she leaves to look for her real mother, to find out more about herself and her family and to try to find that trigger that would bring her memories back. With her new identity: Riley, and her new hair color and glasses, she manages to stay undercover. She finds her mother, but not long after it turns out that she was adopted. The only person who might have an idea about who her real family is is her grandmother, who's with the lorders. Kyala finds some evidence that will help end the lorders but blows her cover doing so, and she's back on the run trying to get the evidence back to Aiden. <br /><br />Shattered is an amazing conclusion to an amazing trilogy! Slated was awesome, Fractured was incredible, but Shattered takes the whole series to a whole new level. So, if you haven't yet picked this series up, I highly suggest you to do it ASAP! It's goddamn worth it!!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4048200101984817360">At first, I thought that Slated would be like all these typical dystopian books about a girl that opposes herself to the regime and becomes part of the revolution, falls in love and in the end, helps to build a new government. While this was definitely a part of the story, it was one of the best dystopian series I've ever read - I finished all three books in two days because I couldn't put it down.<br/>To be honest, all those plot twists and name changes were a bit confusing but when you get to the e</span>
  <span id="freeText4048200101984817360" style="display:none">At first, I thought that Slated would be like all these typical dystopian books about a girl that opposes herself to the regime and becomes part of the revolution, falls in love and in the end, helps to build a new government. While this was definitely a part of the story, it was one of the best dystopian series I've ever read - I finished all three books in two days because I couldn't put it down.<br />To be honest, all those plot twists and name changes were a bit confusing but when you get to the end, it will all make sense! <br />Teri Terry's style of writing is amazing and really adds to the tension of the book.<br />And our main character is developing all the time and is always surprising us and finally discovers who she is - the one thing she wanted to know her whole life.<br />5/5 and I would give more stars if I could.<br />Especially the last book exceeded all my expectations - I often struggled with the last book in the series because they tend to leave me unsatisfied. But not this one. I really loved how geniously everything was connected in this series.</span>

<div id="review_773273369" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/773273369" />
    <a title="Maggie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8410493-maggie"><img alt="Maggie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1355712255p2/8410493.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/773273369?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie" href="/user/show/8410493-maggie">Maggie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399161742" href="/book/show/18667841-shattered">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8410493-maggie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8410493-maggie?shelf=pbook">pbook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8410493-maggie?shelf=library-book">library-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8410493-maggie?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer773273369" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15339179688722670886"><em>This review is going to be divided into two parts, first, my argument for you to read this series if you haven't which will have no spoilers for any of the books in the series, and second, my review of </em>Shattered<em> which will have spoilers for the first two books in the series, but absolutely not spoilers for </em>Shattered<em>.</em><br/><br/>From my review of <em>Slated</em>: "I liked the main character, I liked the idea for the story, and I liked the pacing, but the world building was really terrible and that took away from the </span>
  <span id="freeText15339179688722670886" style="display:none"><em>This review is going to be divided into two parts, first, my argument for you to read this series if you haven't which will have no spoilers for any of the books in the series, and second, my review of </em>Shattered<em> which will have spoilers for the first two books in the series, but absolutely not spoilers for </em>Shattered<em>.</em><br /><br />From my review of <em>Slated</em>: "I liked the main character, I liked the idea for the story, and I liked the pacing, but the world building was really terrible and that took away from the parts of the story that I enjoyed. I wouldn’t not recommend this one, but I also wouldn’t be rushing out to read it."<br /><br />From my review of <em>Fractured</em>: "The world building issues, although still there, were easier to move past in this one and Kyla, who I connected with and liked immensely in the first book, only got better. I tore through the perfect pacing in this one and I’m excited to read the third installment in May. If the third is anywhere near as good as the second I will definitely be making an effort to get more people to read this series."<br /><br />Which begs the question, am I making an effort to get more people to read the <em>Slated </em>series? Hell yes. Lots of people, myself included, like to complain about how series lose steam or how the second book in a trilogy is the weakest, or how an author clearly didn't know how to let go. But what about the opposite? What about when the first book in the series is the weakest? Maybe this is rarer because people are less inclined to give the rest of a series a chance when they struggled with the first one? I still can't exactly explain why I felt compelled to pick up <em>Fractured</em> after all of my problems with <i>Slated</i>, all I can say is that even though I struggled with many things in <em>Slated</em> the story and the characters stayed with me enough that I wanted to find out what happened to them, problems and all.<br /><br />Here are my top three reasons why you should give the <em>Slated</em> series a chance:<br /><br />1. <strong>The Main Character</strong>: It's hard to love a blank slate, but I fell hard for Kyla. At the beginning of the series she's so helpless and clueless, but there's always this spark about her that really comes through. As the series goes on she really comes into her own, even if she might not feel like it, and I really admired her sense of right and wrong and duty to those around her. If you read this series for one reason read it because of Kyla.<br /><br />2. <strong>The World</strong>: How ironic is this? My big issue with the series is the world building, but I'm recommending you read the series because of the world. You will have questions. You will be frustrated. BUT, a lot of what made this story compelling/believable/scary is that the world where it takes place, in the 2060s or 2070s I think (SEE?! I don't even know! ----&gt;poor world building), is so similar to our world. I don't know about anyone else, but when a fake world ties so closely into our own I find the story much more urgent and interesting.<br /><br />3. <strong>The Intricately Woven Story</strong>: This is a complicated story and one that you really need to pay attention to. I think it would be good to read all three of the books together to really be able to dive into the story and remember all the details. But I read all three over the span of a year and that certainly worked too. This is a series where people go away and come back and things over the course of the three books will tie together, which are all things I really like to see in a series.<br /><br />That's my plea for you to read the <i>Slated </i>series and especially to keep reading if you've read the first one and didn't like it or read the first one and don't like it.<br /><br /><em>Below is my review of </em>Shattered<em> which has spoilers for the first two books in the series so if you haven't read them you probably want to stop reading here.</em><br /><br />This will be relatively short. <em>Shattered</em> picks up pretty much where <em>Slated</em> left off, Kyla having escaped from the AGT and Lourders and she's now officially dead, but in fact alive and eager to find out more about her past. Unlike the other two books in the series this one has much less action, much less suspense, and is much more about Kyla figuring out who she is/growing up/coming into her own. Since Kyla is pretty much my favorite part of this series I absolutely loved the chance to get to spend this time with Kyla. And that's kind of all I'm going to say about the story because I don't want to spoil anything for you. But, don't worry, there eventually is action and the book does a good job of wrapping up all of the loose ends of the series.<br /><br />My two issues with the series all along have been the less than stellar world building and the romance. While I wouldn't say the world building improved in this installment there were things about the world that were eventually cleared up and I was left feeling better about the world in general. However, there is something new introduced, a medical-like procedure called IMET that is like a really advanced form of plastic surgery. I was bothered by this because of how similar the rest of the world is to ours. The crazy technology that can so drastically alter how a person looked seemed out of place to me and incongruous with the rest of the story.<br /><br />If you've read my reviews of the first two books in the series you'll know that the romance with Ben did nothing for me. I think I even called Ben something like a wet Slated rag in one of my reviews. I didn't get the romance, to me it was very instalove and young, but after reading <em>Shattered </em>I came away with a better understanding of it and respect for it. To me these books are about Kyla and the romance, even though it was so prominent in the first book, was just a background story that I didn't love.<br /><br /><strong>Bottom Line</strong>: The <em>Slated</em> series is one that really built over the course of the three books and I am so happy I stuck with it after not jiving with the first book in the series. They're probably not books for everyone, but I really came to like and respect them and I hope that people will give them a shot because in the end it's a strong story with a really great main character.<br /><br />This review first appeared on <a href="http://justacouplemorepages.com/2014/07/14/book-review-shattered/" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15339179688722670886" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText5682601484983563886" style="display:none">The Lorders have declare Kyla dead. The young girl is now in hiding under a new identity, Riley Kain (ok now she has like four of them?) <div id="review_672863084" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/672863084" />
    <a title="Alexa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6852982-alexa"><img alt="Alexa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440240098p2/6852982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/672863084?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexa" href="/user/show/6852982-alexa">Alexa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6852982-alexa?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6852982-alexa?shelf=2014-publication">2014-publication</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6852982-alexa?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer672863084" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1483358255707402362">4.5 stars<br/><br/>Such a superb ending to an outstanding trilogy. I'm seriously baffled here, because you <i>can</i> notice that this series was Terry's first project, it is clear that she's an inexperienced author, but despite all of the flaws, she still manages to make these books shine. They're so rich in emotions, it makes you forget anything that you could criticise otherwise.<br/><br/>I had a list of things I wanted this book to address, and I think almost everything on that list was solved. Let's go through it, sh</span>
  <span id="freeText1483358255707402362" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br /><br />Such a superb ending to an outstanding trilogy. I'm seriously baffled here, because you <i>can</i> notice that this series was Terry's first project, it is clear that she's an inexperienced author, but despite all of the flaws, she still manages to make these books shine. They're so rich in emotions, it makes you forget anything that you could criticise otherwise.<br /><br />I had a list of things I wanted this book to address, and I think almost everything on that list was solved. Let's go through it, shall we?<br /><br /><b>1. When Kyla first met Ben, he "looked familiar." Why? Was that some kind of foreshadowing, or nothing? I have a feeling that, perhaps, there's going to be some major plot twist surrounding this.</b><br />Well, okay, no. But then again, it was mentioned once and never again and I guess it was only my own suspicious mind seeing things where there's nothing. <br /><b>2. Nico (duh).</b><br />Yes. There was enough closure with him.<br /><b>3. Kyla's families, both old and new, what happens/happened with them?</b><br />Oh man, don't even get me started. One of the biggest mysteries in this trilogy, but so masterfully done and tied up. I loved it.<br /><b>4. Who reported her missing (again, duh)?</b><br />I'll say more on this later, but: accounted for.<br /><b>5. Doctor Craig?</b><br />Unfortunately, not much is said about him, which is a shame — I still don't know what his role really was in Kyla's past, and we never found out. Oh well.<br /><b>6. Doctor Lysander?</b><br />Yes.<br /><b>7. Cam and Coulson?</b><br />Well, Cam — no, he was not even mentioned once, but Coulson did get his screen time.<br /><b>8. Are Ben and Kyla going to be happy in the end?</b><br />....<br /><b>9. Where's Tori?</b><br />We got our closure.<br /><b>10. Is Aiden a good or a bad guy?</b><br />He's good. <br /><br />So. I'll start off with saying one thing that I am a little bummed about, which is the ending, yes. It came across as a little too easy and sunshiney for the kind of build-up it got, but I think the real thing here is actually, well, something else. I don't want to spoil anything, you know, but I'm just putting it out there that I did not like one thing that was left kind of unresolved.<br /><br />Anyways, I think what I loved best, though, was the relationship between Kyla and her actual mother, Stella, who reported her missing and to whom she returns to at the beginning of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17901410.Shattered__Slated___3_" title="Shattered (Slated, #3) by Teri Terry" rel="nofollow noopener"> Shattered</a>. She doesn't really remember her, so they have to get reacquainted and I thought all of their interactions were just so incredibly <i>raw</i>, it reached out and gripped something in me, shouted <i>This is it, this is so</i> real. Their relationship was so genuine, and Terry simply did a wonderful job at portraying it exactly right: not too much unicorns and rainbows, but also some kind of real reunion with happiness and joy involved. I just ... loved this.<br /><br />Of course, the novel does not lack for mystery and action in the slightest. It was, again, a rollercoaster ride that never let me see too far ahead, which in turn sent me screaming in fear and exhilaration every time the ride took an unexpected turn. Which was lots of times, actually. Bottom line — it was awesome.<br /><br />Character development? Do I have to? I don't have to say a lot, because these characters, as I already mentioned, are so there, they exude an aura and demand so much attention that you can't help but feel like they could step out of the pages every moment. That they <i>should</i> step out at any second. Wonderful.<br /><br />All in all, I'm really sad that this trilogy is over now, but at the same time, it is one of those novels that I'm leaving feeling satisfied, in a way. There are series that I could re-read a hundred times and every time, still turn the last page of the last book and be left like I'm missing something more, which wasn't the case with this book. Yes, there is that one thing that's still nagging at me obviously, but ... yeah. I loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17901410.Shattered__Slated___3_" title="Shattered (Slated, #3) by Teri Terry" rel="nofollow noopener"> Shattered</a>. And I cried, again. I don't know what it is about these three books, but they really resonate with something deep within my soul. I think that this trilogy is one I am going to re-read some time in the future.<br /><br /><a href="http://hellseemscold.blogspot.de/2014/03/review-shattered-by-teri-terry.html" rel="nofollow noopener">This review also appears on my blog.</a><br />____<br />Questions I have that need to be answered:<br /><br />1. When Kyla first met Ben, he "looked familiar." Why? Was that some kind of foreshadowing, or nothing? I have a feeling that, perhaps, there's going to be some major plot twist surrounding this.<br />2. Nico (duh).<br />3. Kyla's families, both old and new, what happens/happened with them?<br />4. Who reported her missing (again, duh)?<br />5. Doctor Craig?<br />6. Doctor Lysander?<br />7. Cam and Coulson?<br />8. Are Ben and Kyla going to be happy in the end?<br />9. Where's Tori?<br />10. Is Aiden a good or a bad guy?<br /><br />Basically. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1483358255707402362" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15401200634852337658" style="display:none">I've had this book for over 6 months and I just knew I can't read it just like that..<br />I knew it's gonna be heavy and horrifying and I was having troubles reading finales to trilogies after Allegiant.<br /><br />I'm half way through and can't decide if that was a good call postponing all that time..<br />In one hand it's unraveling even more shocking truths.. <br />In the other..               <span id="reviewTextContainer809935765" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5392327578396731757">A fantastic end to a great trilogy! This was fast, packed full of action and I just love Kyla as a character. Aiden was great and stepped in over Ben as my favourite male character in the series. Tori absolutely got what she deserved and the ending was so brilliantly satisfying. The story builds up so cleverly from the very first page of Slated and the twists right to the end still surprised me as I read through the 3 books. The characters absolutely drag you into the story and it didn't feel ru</span>
  <span id="freeText5392327578396731757" style="display:none">A fantastic end to a great trilogy! This was fast, packed full of action and I just love Kyla as a character. Aiden was great and stepped in over Ben as my favourite male character in the series. Tori absolutely got what she deserved and the ending was so brilliantly satisfying. The story builds up so cleverly from the very first page of Slated and the twists right to the end still surprised me as I read through the 3 books. The characters absolutely drag you into the story and it didn't feel rushed or contrived at the end like a lot of YA books seem to do. I have been disappointed time and again with half-hearted endings of seemingly good books but Shattered did not disappoint in the least! This trilogy has truly deserved every award it has been given and I am sure I will be reading it over and over again in the future. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5392327578396731757" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('r2QSzjuThEiT1KknOWeA87I4qWpmteAS/hlTsgH8GnDqdUK4TRvd0FiZWSO/h3w2fuP+/UR1SRyRE2NRuqVT2g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

<span id="freeTextContainer9146341074005622402">Teri has lived in France, Canada, Australia and England at more addresses than she can count, acquiring three degrees, a selection of passports and a silly name along the way. The footpaths and canal ways of the Buckinghamshire Chilterns where she now lives inspi</span>
  <span id="freeText9146341074005622402" style="display:none">Teri has lived in France, Canada, Australia and England at more addresses than she can count, acquiring three degrees, a selection of passports and a silly name along the way. Past careers have included scientist, lawyer, optometrist, and, in England, various jobs in schools, libraries and an audiobook charity. The footpaths and canal ways of the Buckinghamshire Chilterns where she now lives inspired much of the setting of Slated. She hates broccoli, likes cats, and has finally worked out what she wants to do when she grows up.<br /><br />Facebook fan page: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/TeriTerryAuthor">http://www.facebook.com/TeriTerryAuthor</a><br />Notes from the Slushpile: group blog on writing for children <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://notesfromtheslushpile.blogspot.co.uk/">http://notesfromtheslushpile.blogspot...</a><br /><br />**IMPORTANT: Please do not message me on Goodreads with requests for review copies, swag, interviews, or anything else. See the contact section of my website for that. Messages on Goodreads may (and probably will) go unanswered!**</span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/25076960-shattered">Quotes from Shattered</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;You, my dear, are getting curiouser and curiouser. Like Alice down the rabbit hole, nothing is as it appears.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/1340687-you-my-dear-are-getting-curiouser-and-curiouser-like-alice">17 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
